  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0aefbfdd-cf76-4321-a46b-22526504b337'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12322103436719941303">Everyone has their rough nights, but things have clearly taken a turn for the surreal when Angel, a young photographer, finds a group of drunken teenagers in the courtyard of his apartment building, taunting a young troll. Trolls are known in Scandinavian mythology as wild beasts like the werewolf, but this troll is just a small, wounded creature. Angel decides to offer it</span>
  <span id="freeText12322103436719941303" style="display:none">Everyone has their rough nights, but things have clearly taken a turn for the surreal when Angel, a young photographer, finds a group of drunken teenagers in the courtyard of his apartment building, taunting a young troll. Trolls are known in Scandinavian mythology as wild beasts like the werewolf, but this troll is just a small, wounded creature. Angel decides to offer it a safe haven for the night. In the morning Angel thinks he dreamed it all. But he finds the troll alive, well, and drinking from his toilet. What does one do with a troll in the city?<br /><br />Angel begins researching frantically. Angel searches the Internet, folklore, nature journals, and newspaper clippings, but his research doesn't tell him that trolls exude pheromones that have a profound aphrodisiac effect on all those around him. As Angel's life changes beyond recognition, it becomes clear that the troll is familiar with the man's most forbidden feelings, and that it may take him across lines he never thought he'd cross. A novel of sparkling originality, Troll is a wry, peculiar, and beguiling story of nature and man's relationship to wild things, and of the dark power of the wildness in ourselves.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12322103436719941303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_33583198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33583198" />
    <a title="David Katzman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1444651-david-katzman"><img alt="David Katzman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399048696p2/1444651.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33583198?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Katzman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Katzman" href="/user/show/1444651-david-katzman">David Katzman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer33583198&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33583198" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13002911551949709472">Well. I must tell you. Two things broke this book to crap for me. Although it was generally rather boring, and I skipped all the alternating chapter of “Troll lore” that were just pointless (despite my love of mythology), and the ludicrous structure that switched so quickly from one character POV to another (in chapters as brief as a paragraph that communicate such deep transitions as “I swung my fist at him.” “His fist hit me in the cheek.”) that they pick up immediately where the other charact</span>
  <span id="freeText13002911551949709472" style="display:none">Well. I must tell you. Two things broke this book to crap for me. Although it was generally rather boring, and I skipped all the alternating chapter of “Troll lore” that were just pointless (despite my love of mythology), and the ludicrous structure that switched so quickly from one character POV to another (in chapters as brief as a paragraph that communicate such deep transitions as “I swung my fist at him.” “His fist hit me in the cheek.”) that they pick up immediately where the other character left off mid-action (must we humiliate ourselves at the alter of Roshomon?), and the “mail order bride” character who lived downstairs and was beaten (don’t care, don’t believe it), and the relationships that were so dysfunctional you don’t like anyone at all, and the majority of characters being so shallow you, again, don’t care, and the fairly flat writing style, and utter lack of humor, and the just-not-quite-convincing behavior of this “troll”, no, it wasn’t all that that broke me on the book, and it certainly wasn’t the perverted troll bestiality-—been there, done that—-nor was it necessarily the offhand reference to a troll by a child as a “black man” when these trolls are, uhm, animalistic wild things and sure, out of the mouths of babes, but to leave a casually racist comment unaddressed for the entirety of a book that’s all about this guy adopting a foundling troll is uncomfortable, but still no, it wasn’t that although I felt that was inexcusable.<br /><br />It was the troll being stuffed into hipster jeans by the main character (commercial photographer) for an ad campaign, and it supposedly being so serious and traumatic when in fact it was just so stupid it was painful. And then finally at the end, the image of papa troll…well, surprise they weren’t so dumb after all. In fact, they stole some guns and know how to use ‘em. And the troll waves the guy into the cave…using the gun like an old time gangsta. Move it buddy, this forest troll’s packin’ heat. This second moment was just so stupid I was embarrassed reading it.<br /><br />What can I say. Unable to suspend belief. And I love the fantastical. Move along people, nothing to read here.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13002911551949709472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38845280" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<div id="review_1684903905" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1684903905" />
    <a title="Alissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24456819-alissa"><img alt="Alissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426345849p2/24456819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684903905?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alissa" href="/user/show/24456819-alissa">Alissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6587394-troll">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24456819-alissa?shelf=read-ebooks">read-ebooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684903905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4561868962895214549">I was very taken with the idea of a fantasy book written by a Finnish author and steeped into Nordic folklore. This story is different from my usual reads (epic/low fantasy) and the worldbuilding is particular, consisting in several explanations, poems or details about trolls and other topics related to the story or the characters reactions to the events, all looking like book extracts. As a literary device to provide background and to further blend the elements of the novel, alongside my intere</span>
  <span id="freeText4561868962895214549" style="display:none">I was very taken with the idea of a fantasy book written by a Finnish author and steeped into Nordic folklore. This story is different from my usual reads (epic/low fantasy) and the worldbuilding is particular, consisting in several explanations, poems or details about trolls and other topics related to the story or the characters reactions to the events, all looking like book extracts. As a literary device to provide background and to further blend the elements of the novel, alongside my interest in them, it succeeded.<br /><br />The first person POVs were also nice and the plot, with its absurd situations the unmoored characters found themselves in quickly felt kind of okay. To a degree at least, because in a nutshell what happens is: guy finds troll, he keeps it as a pet and becomes obsessed. The protagonist’s and the other characters’ lives change dramatically, one way or another, because of the presence of this creature out of myth.<br /><br />It’s hard to identify in any of the characters (thankfully), they all sport peculiar obsessions which factor into the story and the only one who got my sympathy is the guinea pig; I had the impression that I was not supposed to care for any of them, either, as the consequence of a deliberate choice from the author's part, stressed by the compulsive changes of viewpoints and the total lack of character development. The rhythm is slow and the chapters are usually very short, switching back and forth many times during a conversation between the interlocutors.<br /><br />The book gets pretty disturbing halfway through, but a kind of explanation arrives later. It’s a very peculiar work, which deals with a lot of controversial issues (racism, homosexuality, objectification, bride-buying, promiscuity, fixations, a mix of pedophilia and bestiality, brutality....) thrown around like peanuts and often with no purpose that I could discern. I don't judge the depiction but I can’t shake off this feeling of pointlessness. The world is ugly and unfair and selfish, human nature sucks, urban policies will kill us all and people are either slaves of themselves or of someone else; bottom line?<br />I am not sure I liked this book because of all the creepy themes, the flat characters, the vague plot, the so-and-so ending and the narrative flaws, but despite all of this I've read it in a single sitting and that always counts for something.<br /><br /><i>Our city’s unique, but with a slightly different nuance for each of us. In a little town like this, we don’t have our own streets, shops or galleries, but we do have our individual hidden topography, our own street corners.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4561868962895214549" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_454637668" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/454637668" />
    <a title="Kelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3216716-kelley"><img alt="Kelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571196451p2/3216716.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/454637668?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelley" href="/user/show/3216716-kelley">Kelley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3216716-kelley?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3216716-kelley?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer454637668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12253078151863288047">Let me just preface this by saying that this is one of the best novels I've ever read. Prepare for some gushing. I also want to note that I'm an American reader, so a little bit of my fondness might stem from the novelty of being able to read an award-winning Finnish novel that was so wonderfully translated. For me, the book gave the same slightly-distanced feel that foreign movies have, and I love that. This is partially because America really lacks the quantity (and quality) of folklore that i</span>
  <span id="freeText12253078151863288047" style="display:none">Let me just preface this by saying that this is one of the best novels I've ever read. Prepare for some gushing. I also want to note that I'm an American reader, so a little bit of my fondness might stem from the novelty of being able to read an award-winning Finnish novel that was so wonderfully translated. For me, the book gave the same slightly-distanced feel that foreign movies have, and I love that. This is partially because America really lacks the quantity (and quality) of folklore that is present in Finland and necessary for writing a book like Troll. <br /><br />Within a few pages I was hooked because the main character was so sexually charged yet completely androgynous. (Actually, I didn't figure out the main character's gender until a good way into the novel. I think this kept me from drawing my own conclusions and relying on stereotypes, so I had to listen to what Sinisalo had to say about "Angel.") <br /><br />In this book's world, trolls are not merely legends or folklore; they are real and were officially recognized as an animal species in 1907. The book's narration switches from character to character, but it also interrupts itself for brief news articles and folklore readings concerning trolls. These are expertly mixed into the story by the pretense that they are being discovered and read by the main character on his hunt for information. <br /><br />Which brings me to the actual plot of the novel. Angel, a fashion photographer and passionate but unfulfilled person, finds a troll on the way home one night. Being that trolls are extremely rare, and also that this particular one is a "cub" and has been beaten to a pulp by local youths, Angel decides to adopt the creature. So begins a tale of his infatuation with the troll and how this relationship affects his career and personal relationships. It appears that he might actually be able to keep the troll a secret, but there is always the unease left to the reader by the constant switching of narration voice that the troll will be discovered. I honestly thought the troll would die the entire time, but I won't say what did finally happen because I don't want to spoil the ending. I will say that Troll is a melancholy book that somehow manages to be a commentary on society without actually trying. The writing is fantastic, the characters and plot are believable, and it's an easy read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12253078151863288047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1662141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1662141" />
    <a title="Trin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/113980-trin"><img alt="Trin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181029461p2/113980.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1662141?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trin" href="/user/show/113980-trin">Trin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=queerlit">queerlit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=2000s">2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=finnish-lit">finnish-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7587596037502052183">A Finnish book, which is not something I ordinarily get to say. This novel was flawed, but overall I really loved it. It takes place in an alternate universe where trolls were discovered to be a real, living species in the early part of the 20th century. Mikael, a photographer, finds a troll cub who’s somehow stumbled into the city, and takes him in. Their relationship is…not something I can easily describe, but it’s more than a little disturbing, oddly alluring, and completely captivating. The </span>
  <span id="freeText7587596037502052183" style="display:none">A Finnish book, which is not something I ordinarily get to say. This novel was flawed, but overall I really loved it. It takes place in an alternate universe where trolls were discovered to be a real, living species in the early part of the 20th century. Mikael, a photographer, finds a troll cub who’s somehow stumbled into the city, and takes him in. Their relationship is…not something I can easily describe, but it’s more than a little disturbing, oddly alluring, and completely captivating. The narrative—especially the dénouement—is a little rushed, but it was successful in that it left me wanting more but not frustrated with the conclusion. Even the rapidly shifting POV, not something I usually enjoy, worked for me here. According to her bio, Sinisalo has written many other books, but unfortunately this seems to be the only one (besides a short story anthology to which she contributed) that’s been translated into English. How frustrating, because I’d really like to read more of her work. Still, I’m glad I got to read this, and if you can find it—I had to track it down through intramural library loans—I heartily recommend it. It’s unusual and seductive and creepy. One of my favorite combinations!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7587596037502052183" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8819588757064574423">This is one of those books that is hard to describe and oh-so-worthwhile. It's a contemporary urban fantasy and trolls are real creatures. Adopt at own risk.<br/><br/>Then he spends the rest of the book researching how to take care of it. So it's sort of like reading a short story with a whole bunch of reference documents tucked between scenes, but that c</span>
  <span id="freeText8819588757064574423" style="display:none">This is one of those books that is hard to describe and oh-so-worthwhile. It's a contemporary urban fantasy and trolls are real creatures. They are considered animals, and Angel, the main character, finds an abandoned baby troll in the alley. This is presented as like finding a wildcat cub. Adopt at own risk.<br /><br />Then he spends the rest of the book researching how to take care of it. So it's sort of like reading a short story with a whole bunch of reference documents tucked between scenes, but that comes nowhere near describing the emotional impact of the whole. Especially the last chapter. <br /><br />Recommended.</span>

<div id="review_3318025" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3318025" />
    <a title="_inbetween_" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/105717-inbetween"><img alt="_inbetween_" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180515629p2/105717.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3318025?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="_inbetween_" class="user" itemprop="url" name="_inbetween_" href="/user/show/105717-inbetween">_inbetween_</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3318025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3581470787692676755">For once, a synopsis, because I had never seen one (that actually said what Troll was about/happened in it): "Angel" (Mikael, gay photographer) takes in an abandonned Troll-puppy, which is described like a cat (believe me, I know, down to the litter), though Sinisalo lists good (fake) snippets how it is a recently discovered species of ape-cat (cp. the Okapi). Sinisalo uses real sources as well, most notably Pelli + Illusia (Angel with his head of blond curls so much like Illusia (a fairy) even </span>
  <span id="freeText3581470787692676755" style="display:none">For once, a synopsis, because I had never seen one (that actually said what Troll was about/happened in it): "Angel" (Mikael, gay photographer) takes in an abandonned Troll-puppy, which is described like a cat (believe me, I know, down to the litter), though Sinisalo lists good (fake) snippets how it is a recently discovered species of ape-cat (cp. the Okapi). Sinisalo uses real sources as well, most notably Pelli + Illusia (Angel with his head of blond curls so much like Illusia (a fairy) even calls "his" troll Pelli), and since Troll isn't sensational and often slow, the fake info seems persuasively real.<br />At the start of the book, Angel loves Martes, a "straight" gay who secretly enjoys having Angel lust after him, while Angel's ex "Spiderman", a vet, still loves Angel, as does Ecke (the guy that I liked in this book, short, messy, broad ass, glasses) and Palomita, a tiny young girl from the Philippines, mail-order bride, sex-slave. <br />Her fate just hit me so deep that for most of the book, I could not concentrate on the - much tinier than expected - "erotic" Troll love, but I dislike her for her final act, which made it clear to me that the theme of the novel is less "A Lovestory" or how the wild(erness) encroaches and how people like Palomita's "husband" and the vile Martes really are "trolls", no, for me it was about people using each other.<br />I'm actually pretty sure that wasn't intentional, but Angel uses Ecke and Spiderman, even if that gives those two greatest pleasure and exactly what they want (sex with Angel (sorry, hardly anything described)), so they in turn are using Angel. Advertising guy Martes uses Angel despicably, Palomita is obviously used, the Troll is used - though he of course triumphs in the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3581470787692676755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3467789453" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3467789453" />
    <a title="Dawn C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14948447-dawn-c"><img alt="Dawn C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535435406p2/14948447.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3467789453?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawn C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawn C" href="/user/show/14948447-dawn-c">Dawn C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14948447-dawn-c?shelf=loved">loved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14948447-dawn-c?shelf=fairytale-mythology">fairytale-mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3467789453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2695839847752033395">Troll: A Love Story, or “Not Before Sundown” as the original title is (and every other translation sticks to but the American) is a fascinating sort of modern folklore/mythology/horror story about a guy who finds an injured young troll, brings it home and nutures it back to life with life changing consequences. Trolls are in the universe of this novel real but rare creatures in Northern Scandinavia, and our guy, Angel, spends the first days researching what a troll eats while trying to keep its </span>
  <span id="freeText2695839847752033395" style="display:none">Troll: A Love Story, or “Not Before Sundown” as the original title is (and every other translation sticks to but the American) is a fascinating sort of modern folklore/mythology/horror story about a guy who finds an injured young troll, brings it home and nutures it back to life with life changing consequences. Trolls are in the universe of this novel real but rare creatures in Northern Scandinavia, and our guy, Angel, spends the first days researching what a troll eats while trying to keep its present a secret from neighbors and lovers.<br /><br />The story is told from the perspectives of various characters with each their intent and persona, varying in length, and sprinkled with articles, old sagas and songs and news snippets about trolls. This narrative works extremely well for me, it’s one of my favorite ways of writing, and it worked really well with this type of story. A truly unique little gem.<br /><br />I definitely want to read more by Johanna Sinisalo, sadly it seems only one other book of hers has been translated. Hopefully that’ll change.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2695839847752033395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_229605830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229605830" />
    <a title="Ryandake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4057623-ryandake"><img alt="Ryandake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280111549p2/4057623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229605830?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryandake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryandake" href="/user/show/4057623-ryandake">Ryandake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229605830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4430934605554678711">oh now here's a lovely one.<br/><br/>i was hooked by the first paragraph--a description of a young man flirting with another, wanting to hold hands and being subtly rejected. perfectly described--not overblown or sentimental, but with feeling. perfect.<br/><br/>and the rest of the story is like that, too. how a man falls for a troll. his efforts to care for the young, unwell troll. how his world begins to spin around the animal, and how it changes his life.<br/><br/>the ending is pitch-perfect too--tragic but inevitable, and</span>
  <span id="freeText4430934605554678711" style="display:none">oh now here's a lovely one.<br /><br />i was hooked by the first paragraph--a description of a young man flirting with another, wanting to hold hands and being subtly rejected. perfectly described--not overblown or sentimental, but with feeling. perfect.<br /><br />and the rest of the story is like that, too. how a man falls for a troll. his efforts to care for the young, unwell troll. how his world begins to spin around the animal, and how it changes his life.<br /><br />the ending is pitch-perfect too--tragic but inevitable, and hopeful as well. not in a schmaltzy hollywood way, either. in the way of life as we live it.<br /><br />there <i>is</i> a bit much troll lore, some of it misplaced, but all of it functioning to further and deepen the plot. so skim it if it gets to be too much, but be careful--you might miss something important. note to would-be authors: excerpting stuff written in a dry, academic style is still stuff written in a dry, academic style, even if it's fictional dry, academic stuff.<br /><br />i wholeheartedly recommend it all the same. you won't be disappointed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4430934605554678711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127403515" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127403515" />
    <a title="Becca Silvers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4449424-becca-silvers"><img alt="Becca Silvers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287756702p2/4449424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127403515?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becca Silvers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becca Silvers" href="/user/show/4449424-becca-silvers">Becca Silvers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127403515" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1580642157283344838">I didn't hate the book but I did hate a lot about it. I dislike in general when books are written from many different points of view, and this one seemed particularly hard to follow because of it. Characters are referred to by several different names so I cant even keep track of whose point of view it was in relation to what they've been a part of in the past. <br/><br/>Plus I got a sick feeling that the only reason the author made the main character, Angel, gay, was to make the leap to bestiality/pedophi</span>
  <span id="freeText1580642157283344838" style="display:none">I didn't hate the book but I did hate a lot about it. I dislike in general when books are written from many different points of view, and this one seemed particularly hard to follow because of it. Characters are referred to by several different names so I cant even keep track of whose point of view it was in relation to what they've been a part of in the past. <br /><br />Plus I got a sick feeling that the only reason the author made the main character, Angel, gay, was to make the leap to bestiality/pedophilia. I found that tacky and ignorant, even though that may not have been the authors intention. <br /><br />I found the character of Palomita depressing and irrelevant, unless to show that humans are often treated as animals even in the modern day, perhaps hinting that one day trolls will be treated as humans by everyone. <br /><br />Glad I read it but I have no desire to read anything else by this author. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1580642157283344838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_311732602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311732602" />
    <a title="Ancestral Gaidheal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal"><img alt="Ancestral Gaidheal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591295461p2/1544974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311732602?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ancestral Gaidheal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ancestral Gaidheal" href="/user/show/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal">Ancestral Gaidheal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal?shelf=myths">myths</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal?shelf=finland">finland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal?shelf=for-sale">for-sale</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1544974-ancestral-gaidheal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311732602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3631301507251338321"><b>Why did I read it?</b> It came up a few times on recommended lists and a book which featured a troll by a Finnish writer seemed like an interesting read, even when the synopsis hinted at sexual themes.<br/><br/><b>What's it about?</b> Mikael is returning from a gay club one evening and intercepts a gang intent on beating a cornered animal. Upon seeing the victim, it becomes clear to Mikael it is a young troll and, intoxicated by liquor and the beauty of the troll itself, he takes it home with him. Mikael attempts to</span>
  <span id="freeText3631301507251338321" style="display:none"><b>Why did I read it?</b> It came up a few times on recommended lists and a book which featured a troll by a Finnish writer seemed like an interesting read, even when the synopsis hinted at sexual themes.<br /><br /><b>What's it about?</b> Mikael is returning from a gay club one evening and intercepts a gang intent on beating a cornered animal. Upon seeing the victim, it becomes clear to Mikael it is a young troll and, intoxicated by liquor and the beauty of the troll itself, he takes it home with him. Mikael attempts to restore the troll to health by reading all sorts of materials, but never seems aware of the intoxicating pheromones the troll exudes, and which come to mingle with his own scent.<br /><br /><b>What did I like?</b> It's a different kind of fantasy I suppose. The chapters were short, making it a quick read and, once again, the ending isn't neatly tied up. I was a little interested in the fate of the troll, and some of the snippets of information inserted between chapters were intriguing.<br /><br />The portrayal of the futility of attempting to tame an animal which thrives in the wild was quite well done. The story also highlights the increasing urbanisation of previously wild environments which is forcing many an animal/creature to adapt and survive on our terms, and how much mankind/humans are adverse to this encroachment by "wild things" on what they consider their turf.<br /><br /><b>What didn't I like?</b> "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7961609.Not_Before_Sundown" title="Not Before Sundown by Johanna Sinisalo" rel="nofollow noopener">Not Before Sundown</a>" as it's also known, just didn't grab me. I stopped caring about Mikael, or what fate awaited him fairly early in the story, when his tiresome selfish/self-centered personality was revealed. Eventually, the <i>factual</i> accounts, snippets of folklore and various bits of information regarding trolls which was inserted between chapters also became tedious. Thus, the book dragged itself, limping, to it's conclusion[?].<br /><br />Certain aspects of Mikael's behaviour were also very off-putting; more particularly, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his sexual feelings towards Pessi, the troll <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br /><b>Would I recommend it?</b> I can't say I would, mostly because I cannot think of anyone who should enjoy reading it; certainly no-one of my acquaintance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3631301507251338321" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5581681575874453175" style="display:none">This book had been mentioned by someone whose own writing I like quite a lot. It was a selection included in a creative writing course that he was teaching. In fairness, I never heard him say if he liked it or not, but wow - what a relentless bombardment of puerile drivel! I liked the troll, what little of him I got to see. Hated every other character in the (first half of)(far as I could get)the book. This is one of those books that I would like to physically throw just as far away from me as I could, but alas - it's in my Kindle. It shall be electronically-jettisoned, I assure you, but that simply doesn't pack the same enjoyment one gets from hurling a physical tome. <br /><br />But hell - you might like it - who knows.</span>

<div id="review_3525634452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3525634452" />
    <a title="Stacia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3917029-stacia"><img alt="Stacia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316011190p2/3917029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3525634452?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia" href="/user/show/3917029-stacia">Stacia</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3917029-stacia?shelf=europe">europe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3917029-stacia?shelf=2020">2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3525634452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8723817438042292320">Um... that was... unique.<br/><br/>I like weird, unusual, & unique books. And this one has some positives. But, there are also deeper negatives that I'm still trying to unpack (old racist tropes; bestiality; sex slave & domestic violence; more).<br/><br/>It's a pretty quick read & I read it in one sitting. Even though parts were somewhat touching or intriguing, there are bigger pieces scratching at my brain, bothering me. <br/><br/>I think Bogi Takács' <a href='https://www.tor.com/2018/07/31/quiltbag-speculative-classics-troll-a-love-story-by-johanna-sinisalo' rel='nofollow noopener'>review on Tor.com</a> sums up a lot of the same thoughts I have on this book.</span>
  <span id="freeText8723817438042292320" style="display:none">Um... that was... unique.<br /><br />I like weird, unusual, &amp; unique books. And this one has some positives. But, there are also deeper negatives that I'm still trying to unpack (old racist tropes; bestiality; sex slave &amp; domestic violence; more).<br /><br />It's a pretty quick read &amp; I read it in one sitting. Even though parts were somewhat touching or intriguing, there are bigger pieces scratching at my brain, bothering me. <br /><br />I think Bogi Takács' <a href="https://www.tor.com/2018/07/31/quiltbag-speculative-classics-troll-a-love-story-by-johanna-sinisalo" rel="nofollow noopener">review on Tor.com</a> sums up a lot of the same thoughts I have on this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8723817438042292320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2102615" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2102615" />
    <a title="Sean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/138600-sean"><img alt="Sean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562511132p2/138600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2102615?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean" href="/user/show/138600-sean">Sean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those with a strong taste for the homoerotic.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138600-sean?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138600-sean?shelf=glbtq2-interest">glbtq2-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138600-sean?shelf=non-us">non-us</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138600-sean?shelf=translation">translation</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2102615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3583897238288711195">Johanna Sinisalo is apparently well-known in Finland. It's too bad the only pieces of hers that we have in English are this book and a short story in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/678471.The_Dedalus_Book_of_Finnish_Fantasy__Dedalus_Literary_Fantasy_Anthologies_' title='The Dedalus Book of Finnish Fantasy (Dedalus Literary Fantasy Anthologies) by Johanna Sinisalo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dedalus Book of Finnish Fantasy</a> (which I have yet to read). But if <i>Troll</i> is representative of her writing, I have high, high hopes for more of her work.<br/><br/><i>Troll</i> plays with several kinds of eroticism and desire as we see the central story unfold: Angel, a gay photographer, rescues a young, injured troll from a band of teenage tormenters and takes i</span>
  <span id="freeText3583897238288711195" style="display:none">Johanna Sinisalo is apparently well-known in Finland. It's too bad the only pieces of hers that we have in English are this book and a short story in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/678471.The_Dedalus_Book_of_Finnish_Fantasy__Dedalus_Literary_Fantasy_Anthologies_" title="The Dedalus Book of Finnish Fantasy (Dedalus Literary Fantasy Anthologies) by Johanna Sinisalo" rel="nofollow noopener">Dedalus Book of Finnish Fantasy</a> (which I have yet to read). But if <i>Troll</i> is representative of her writing, I have high, high hopes for more of her work.<br /><br /><i>Troll</i> plays with several kinds of eroticism and desire as we see the central story unfold: Angel, a gay photographer, rescues a young, injured troll from a band of teenage tormenters and takes it home to nurse it. The situation is complicated by a series of encounters and a maze of desire and lust. Who desires whom and why becomes very important as the story reaches its climax. Throughout, Sinisalo has inserted bits of Finnish troll lore—partly authentic, partly invented—that lend a confident air of realism to the novel. Above all, this is less a fantasy than a novel of an alternate Finland where trolls (<i>Felipithecus trollius</i>) really do exist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3583897238288711195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1543294601" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543294601" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11891868-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462459682p2/11891868.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1543294601?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/11891868-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781555847371" href="/book/show/10254265-troll">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543294601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17088045832617151219">I'm not sure why, but I went into this one expecting a kind of twisted/playful dark comedy. That's not at all what this book is -- in fact there is pretty much no humor at all. In addition there were a number of other annoyances:<br/><br/>- the erratic and often pointless jumps in POV<br/>- the fictional history/folklore, which started out interesting but eventually seemed like the author was just trying to pad the page count<br/>- the seemingly blatant connections being made between homosexuality, bestiality, and </span>
  <span id="freeText17088045832617151219" style="display:none">I'm not sure why, but I went into this one expecting a kind of twisted/playful dark comedy. That's not at all what this book is -- in fact there is pretty much no humor at all. In addition there were a number of other annoyances:<br /><br />- the erratic and often pointless jumps in POV<br />- the fictional history/folklore, which started out interesting but eventually seemed like the author was just trying to pad the page count<br />- the seemingly blatant connections being made between homosexuality, bestiality, and pedophilia<br />- much of the writing was kind of generally wooden, although this might be the fault of the translator.<br />- the ending was a bit bizarre, not in a good way. What we learned about the troll throughout the novel just didn't really support what happened.<br /><br />Despite this laundry list, in the end I don't think I disliked it quite enough to give it only one star. It moved at a brisk pace, which is an especially good quality in a book when you're not enjoying it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17088045832617151219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1510545861" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1510545861" />
    <a title="Phyllis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19228026-phyllis"><img alt="Phyllis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547871251p2/19228026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1510545861?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Phyllis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Phyllis" href="/user/show/19228026-phyllis">Phyllis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510545861" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9820356695079443017">This is a unique and original book about a young troll who was being tormented by a group of teens. Angel, a photographer finds him and rescues him. But the troll is a wild animal. I'm not sure if it's a myth, legend, dark adult fairy tale or fable. The setting is in Finland which is part of the reason I chose it. Johanna Sinisalo is a very talented author. This is one of those books that will stay with me for a long time. 4.5 stars</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2767557209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2767557209" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7356675-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1326055016p2/7356675.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2767557209?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/7356675-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7356675-stephen?shelf=2019-popsugar-challenge">2019-popsugar-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7356675-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2767557209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13297262681424213010">I don't think this book is homophobic. I think the author just hates her characters. It is the kind of literary style (not the somewhat whimsical story I was hoping for, given the title) where likable characters aren't considered necessary (though it would help if they had some dimensions).<br/><br/>The main character Angel is, I'm going with, a complete asshole. The idea of bringing a Troll--which in this world is a wild animal--into his home is bad enough--though that could just be idiocy. But the main </span>
  <span id="freeText13297262681424213010" style="display:none">I don't think this book is homophobic. I think the author just hates her characters. It is the kind of literary style (not the somewhat whimsical story I was hoping for, given the title) where likable characters aren't considered necessary (though it would help if they had some dimensions).<br /><br />The main character Angel is, I'm going with, a complete asshole. The idea of bringing a Troll--which in this world is a wild animal--into his home is bad enough--though that could just be idiocy. But the main character isn't willing to reveal the troll's existence to anyone else, even when it won't eat, even when it's dying of parasites. Because apparently, he'd rather have the poor animal die than have it moved to a zoo or whatever else.<br /><br />And if that isn't bad enough, the main character, who is an advertising photographer hired for a new jeans company, forces his pet troll into a pair of jeans so he can take pictures of the poor guy screaming and trying to rip them off so he can make big bucks in an ad camp. Of course, the poor Troll is suffering from Stockholm syndrome (or Helsinki Syndrome, given this is in Finland), or maybe pheremones (which are way way overpowered in this book). So, yeah, asshole.<br /><br />The other point of views men in the book are any better--we just don't get to see as much of them to find out how bad they are. But generally they all try to trick each other, usually for sex, sometimes for money. The single point o view woman is a Filipina mail-order bride who should be sympathetic but, honestly, the descriptions of her life feel too clinical to make the reader care.<br /><br />But even if this is just a book that hates it's characters because people are disgusting, not because they're gay or for any other attribute, I'm still surprised that this was nominated for a Gaylactic Spectrum Award and won a Tiptree. (I would be more surprised if I couldn't name a Lambda Award winner from the past year that's transphobic, albeit probably unintentionally so). Angel feels like a stereotype, especially with his promiscuity (the only POV character he doesn't have sex with or try hard to have sex with is the women) and, FFS, how he slips toward bestiality. I will say the quote from Le Guin on the Tiptree page is surprisingly ambivalent given it's about the award winner. And a quote from another juror (?) on that page is shockingly gender essentialist about how this book "reveals the life of the human male" (isn't this the Tiptree???) but then again this is an award given 15 years ago, and I'm hear to review the book, not the Awards the book won.<br /><br />Even though this wasn't the whimsical book the title made me hope for, there were still elements that drew me in. In this world Trolls are real animals, not fantastic ones, living in small numbers, mostly remote from human life, discovered relatively late by science. It's as if we got to explore the real existence of a not-quite human species, like Sasquatch or Yeti being found to be real. Much of the book is made up of mythology, in world science, or oher accounts of trolls making for a fascinating world. Unfortunately the story itself is best avoided.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13297262681424213010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21617155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21617155" />
    <a title="FicusFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1104480-ficusfan"><img alt="FicusFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1209956626p2/1104480.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21617155?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="FicusFan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="FicusFan" href="/user/show/1104480-ficusfan">FicusFan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1104480-ficusfan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1104480-ficusfan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1104480-ficusfan?shelf=myths">myths</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1104480-ficusfan?shelf=read-2009">read-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1104480-ficusfan?shelf=read-10-09">read-10-09</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer21617155&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21617155" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12527371813988543696">I read this book for a RL book group. I had already picked it up because it had such hype when it came out. I let it sit for a couple of years, and then read it for my group. I really wanted to like it more, but it was rather meh, disjointed and even a bit beyond the pale in some connections its makes. <br/><br/>The story is of a young man who is full of himself. He is a photographer, gay, and personally and professionally hot. He is called Angel, but his real name is Michael. Those in his circle hang out</span>
  <span id="freeText12527371813988543696" style="display:none">I read this book for a RL book group. I had already picked it up because it had such hype when it came out. I let it sit for a couple of years, and then read it for my group. I really wanted to like it more, but it was rather meh, disjointed and even a bit beyond the pale in some connections its makes. <br /><br />The story is of a young man who is full of himself. He is a photographer, gay, and personally and professionally hot. He is called Angel, but his real name is Michael. Those in his circle hang out at this cafe and their interactions are like soap operas. He loves someone, who is leading him on and then saying he is not gay; he is loved by others, whom he doesn't even recognize as existing. <br /><br />One night he is going home and he finds some thuggish teens trying to beat up a small young troll. In this story, though set in modern day Finland, trolls are real. They live in the woods and usually keep away from humans. <br /><br />Angel adopts the troll, and takes him into his home, and eventually his heart. He names him Pessi. The story follows Angel as he tries to save the troll who is sick at first and then to teach him how to live with humans and in an apartment rather than the wild. Angel becomes strangely attached to him, and plans to keep him, rather than returning him to the forest. Eventually Angel uses him as a model in a photographic spread that becomes wildly successful. The success has a dramatic impact on Angel's human relationships. Pessi and Angel's relationship wanders into forbidden territory and leads to bloodshed.<br /><br />The writing was fine. Often a translation has issues, but I don't think the problems can be blamed on the translator. <br /><br />First the story was broken up with little insets of information about trolls. There was religious, historical, folkloric, even scientific information. It was helpful and interesting, but it made the story choppy and lacking in cohesion. Towards the end of the story the insets become newspaper stories about crimes and gun killings of humans in and around the forest.<br /> <br />Second, I really didn't get the characters, and certainly didn't care anything about them. It didn't help that some were referred to by more than one name, so you weren't really sure who was who. They were really self-absorbed and rather flat, not like real people. The guys were all playing games. <br /><br />The one woman, a downstairs neighbor and mail order Filipina bride, was barely able to communicate. She was also beaten, downtrodden, and living in fear of her abusive husband. She had a strange fantasy relationship with Angel, mistaking his kindness for interest. I really have no idea why she is even in the story at all. Perhaps to show a human who is living and being treated like an animal, with Pessi an animal, living and being treated like a person. In any event she is the only developed character to me.<br /><br />Pessi doesn't really have a personality to me, and he is ill-defined, perhaps deliberately. The informational insets clearly call him an animal, but the folkloric ones say that at time the Fins treat trolls as people. Angel begins to have a strong emotional attachment, that hints at a physical relationship.<br /><br />The connections of having a gay character flirt with bestiality as though its no big deal, I find troubling. Even worse is the way Pessi is portrayed as being able to pass as a young boy. So now we have connected gay, bestiality, and pedophilia, as though they are all different aspects of the same thing. Perhaps that wasn't the author's intent, but that was the impression I got as I read the book. The racist 'Black Man' comment is also not cool, but perhaps the author is unaware of the implications of calling an animal a black man.<br /><br />The ending was just odd, and wandered into fantasy. it did leave you wondering though.<br /><br />I just didn't really enjoy the book all that much.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12527371813988543696" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1181041216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1181041216" />
    <a title="Voldemort" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10777452-voldemort"><img alt="Voldemort" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518705352p2/10777452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1181041216?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Voldemort" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Voldemort" href="/user/show/10777452-voldemort">Voldemort</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777452-voldemort?shelf=21st-century">21st-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777452-voldemort?shelf=bizarre-but-fascinating">bizarre-but-fascinating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10777452-voldemort?shelf=uh-la-la-uh-la-la">uh-la-la-uh-la-la</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1181041216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14709470944604528093">3.5<br/><br/>I've always asked myself; why do I end up reading weird books? Followed usually by another question; why do I end up liking weird books? And there's always that other question; Is something wrong with me?<br/>Sadly I can't answer them. Yet.<br/>If I could summarize the book it would be easy simple words. <br/>Gay guy falls in love with troll. Murder. Blood. Gore. Ejaculation. Gay guy and troll run away. End. <br/>Meaningless shit unless you're Freud. The author must have had some incredible major balls (metaphor</span>
  <span id="freeText14709470944604528093" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />I've always asked myself; why do I end up reading weird books? Followed usually by another question; why do I end up liking weird books? And there's always that other question; Is something wrong with me?<br />Sadly I can't answer them. Yet.<br />If I could summarize the book it would be easy simple words. <br />Gay guy falls in love with troll. Murder. Blood. Gore. Ejaculation. Gay guy and troll run away. End. <br />Meaningless shit unless you're Freud. The author must have had some incredible major balls (metaphorical balls, she's a woman) to write this kind of story, it's pretty much taboo although nowadays we did discover some individuals getting it on with cows... or goats... or chickens. <br />The subject is definitely original however the prose is hideous; it steals from encyclopedias, internet, documents, myths, tales, other books a little too much for my taste, it almost loses its fictional side and yet it keeps the originality somehow. The information is abundant and I rather liked it because I've never really googled trolls or why do trolls live in Finland or why do we call internet trolls trolls... wait, I might have googled the last one. If somebody had asked me about trolls years ago I'd have shrieked out loud "Trolls, trolls in the dungeons". Apparently they're more like felines and less like Hagrid. Which is fine. <br />So why like this scary creepy bizarre book if not for the literary values? <br />Because it's raw, instinctual, primitive in its sexual appeal and true. There were pheromones in every page trying to find their way out, sticking into my skin and all I could smell was a tiny whiff of melted butter coming from my body. My pheromones probably. <br />There was this quote I enjoyed; He tried to possess the forest, yet the forest possessed him instead. <br />I tried to dislike the book yes, but I'm half sure the book disliked me in the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14709470944604528093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9NMO7z9pzUvOGikOdBNrFOZ//AxUlCLBJJ5rP339+uf6psMp4cYJg/n0C14vkTA59HDQk4uddjl5PFmyBYlBxw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0ZKSYaKzCrRR2smMkrYS64Z3FQOtBRqgQhn8TRtYoqnf51+nfBzOfGY069zJNEnGlHg5nHIMTlgfu87AYywZiQ==')})
  }

The crowning accomplishment of Finland\'s first literary genius, Seven Brothers remains &quot;the greatest Finnish novel of all time&quot;, the classic among the classics in Finnish literature. Published in 1870, in the author\'s 36th year and two years before his untimely death, Seven Brothers laid the foundation for what Kai Laitinen later called &quot;The Great Tradition in Finnish Prose&quot;. This tradition is characterized by realism, humor, respect for the common people, and depiction of nature as both friend and foe. Received at the time of publication by uncomprehending arbiters of literary taste, who still delighted in romantic approaches to literature, Seven Brothers fared poorly in early reviews.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/58013.Johanna_Sinisalo">About Johanna Sinisalo</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/58013.Johanna_Sinisalo"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1237901165p3/58013.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/58013.Johanna_Sinisalo">Johanna Sinisalo
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
217
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer340736590653292892">ENG: Johanna Sinisalo is an award-winning Finnish author. She was born in Sodankylä in 1958. During 1984-1997, she worked as a professional designer in advertising, after which she started as a screenwriter and writer. Sinisalo's first novel, <i>Troll</i>, won the Finlandia prize, the most important literature award in Finland. As her hobbies, Sinisalo mentions astronomy, gastronomy, hiking, literature a</span>
  <span id="freeText340736590653292892" style="display:none">ENG: Johanna Sinisalo is an award-winning Finnish author. She was born in Sodankylä in 1958. During 1984-1997, she worked as a professional designer in advertising, after which she started as a screenwriter and writer. Sinisalo's first novel, <i>Troll</i>, won the Finlandia prize, the most important literature award in Finland. As her hobbies, Sinisalo mentions astronomy, gastronomy, hiking, literature and comics.<br /><br />The author notes that her novels always feature a bit of the small everyday reality. However, overcoming the borders of realism does not mean that the author's works were to be classified as sci-fi or fantasy – from Sinisalo's point of view, categorizing literature by genre should be left behind. <br /><br />FI: Johanna Sinisalo on syntynyt Sodankylässä vuonna 1958. Hän valmistui ylioppilaaksi Tampereella 1977 ja suoritti kandidaatintutkinnon Tampereen yliopiston yleisen kirjallisuustieteen draamalinjalla vuonna 1986. Markkinointi-instituutissa opiskellessaan hän sai vuoden parhaan diplomityön palkinnon 1987. Vuosina 1984–1997 Sinisalo toimi ammatikseen mainonnan suunnittelijana, sittemmin hän ryhtyi vapaaksi käsikirjoittajaksi ja kirjailijaksi. Sinisalon esikoisromaani <i>Ennen päivänlaskua ei voi</i> voitti vuoden 2000 Finlandia-palkinnon. Sittemmin Sinisalo on saanut muun muassa James Tiptree Jr. -palkinnon, Tampereen kaupungin kirjallisuuspalkinnon ja Prometheus-palkinnon.<br /><br />Kirjailijan perheeseen kuuluu avomies ja aikuinen tytär. Harrastuksikseen Sinisalo mainitsee tähtitieteen, gastronomian, vaelluksen, kirjallisuuden ja sarjakuvan. Sinisalo asuu lapsuutensa kotikaupungissa Tampereella. <br /><br />Tärkeitä kirjailijoita Sinisalolle ovat olleet Tove Jansson, Astrid Lindgren, L. M. Montgomery, Ray Bradbury, Volter Kilpi, Vladimir Nabokov, Michel Tournier ja Margaret Atwood. Tieteiskirjallisuuden lukemisen Sinisalo aloitti lapsena Edgar Rice Burroughsin seikkailukirjoilla. Niiden jälkeen hän löysi George Orwellin ja Aldous Huxleyn, joiden teoksissa science fiction on yhteiskunnan havainnoinin ja arvostelun väline.<br /><br />Kirjailija toteaa, että hänen romaaneissaan on aina jokin pieni piirre arkitodellisuuden ulkopuolelta. Sinisalo on useiden muiden tavoin muistuttanut, että puhdas realismi on varsin nuori, 1800-luvun lopulta peräisin oleva kirjallinen suuntaus. Realismin rajojen ylittäminen ei kuitenkaan tarkoita, että kirjailijan teokset olisivat lajityypiltään scifiä tai fantasiaa. Sinisalon mielestä lajityyppiajattelusta pitäisi irtautua.<br /><br />Sinisalo painottaa, että spekulatiivisuus ei ole kirjallisuudessa itseisarvo, vaan että sen kautta voidaan sanoa jotain oleellista jopa paremmin kuin realismin keinoin. Fantasian tai science fictionin kirjoittaminen ei ole päämäärä vaan väline kirjallisuuden tuottamiseen. Sinisalo käyttää sanaa ”viistovalaistus” kuvaamaan tämän välineen toimintaa: todellisuuden tutkiminen uudesta ja ennenkokemattomasta näkökulmasta voi paljastaa uusia puolia, joita ei ole voinut aikaisemmin nähdä.</span>
  <a data-text-id="340736590653292892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2995200-ennen-p-iv-nlaskua-ei-voi">Quotes from Troll: A Love Story</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Like that breeder-woman sitting at the bar, who thinks it's a buzz to go into a gay joint and has no doubt heard somewhere that this is one. Her lurid get-up's a joke, ludicrous. She's the type who dons the camouflage-green combat trousers, wraps a bandanna around her head and paints herself with black lipstick, imagining all the lesbians in the joint'll have the hots for her. Not so much imagining as secretly hoping. <br /><br />Naturally, no one goes and sits with her. She's been here before, and everyone gives the ice-cold shoulder, yet she still turns up again and again. Someone might argue we're zoo animals for her. But I've another theory. For her, we're noble savages, a kind of grey area outside the respectable, minutely organized community, an untamed wilderness it takes a lot of guts to step into. But if you do dare, there's a glorious smell of freedom floating around your trousers and giving the finger to society, making whoever an instant anarchist. Certainly, for her, coming here is like putting a washable tattoo on your shoulder : there's the thrill of deviance with none of the dull commitment - and she'll never have to wonder whether she's too weird to be seen out before dark.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/617928-like-that-breeder-woman-sitting-at-the-bar-who-thinks-it-s">8 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;It is said, once a wise man from the far North told me; it is said that there are in certain parts of Scandinavia cities within cities like there are circles within circles; existent yet invisible. And those cities are inhabited by creatures more terrible than imagination can create : man-shaped but man-devouring, as black and as silent as the night they prowl in.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/7974614-it-is-said-once-a-wise-man-from-the-far">2 likes</a>
            </nobr>

          </div>
